<div id="review_2853818942" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2853818942" />
    <a title="Cheryl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3498889-cheryl"><img alt="Cheryl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590863781p2/3498889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2853818942?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheryl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheryl" href="/user/show/3498889-cheryl">Cheryl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780679441557" href="/book/show/77702.Ladder_of_Years">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2853818942" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5414729161217047472">I'm surprised by how much I enjoyed this story and these characters. At first I was annoyed with Delia for being so self-centered, for not attempting to truly understand her loved ones, for thinking that all they said and did was a reflection of their interactions with her. But gradually & subtly she, and we, learn more about their inner lives. <br/>By the time the book ended, I *still* wasn't sure just how it was going to... even though I read carefully, fully absorbed, savoringly. And even when I l</span>
  <span id="freeText5414729161217047472" style="display:none">I'm surprised by how much I enjoyed this story and these characters. At first I was annoyed with Delia for being so self-centered, for not attempting to truly understand her loved ones, for thinking that all they said and did was a reflection of their interactions with her. But gradually &amp; subtly she, and we, learn more about their inner lives. <br />By the time the book ended, I *still* wasn't sure just how it was going to... even though I read carefully, fully absorbed, savoringly. And even when I learned the ending, I had to think about it. I'm still not sure it was the ending *I* wanted, but it's the best for these characters.*<br /><br />And Tyler makes it all look effortless. The theme of second chances in love is expressed in so many different characters' lives, in so many different shapes &amp; styles, it feels like we're reading several stories at once. In that way, it somewhat resembles a Maeve Binchy book - but it's even better.<br />Tyler is such a good writer. All the details she drops in with such studied casualness make it easy to feel as if one knows the characters as real people. A ginger jar in the B.B Dr's waiting room, the twins' dresses the color of Crest fluoride toothpaste, buying barley for gripe water (I never heard of it before, but from those two sentences I know I want to make it).<br /><br />Walking with a two year-old, at his pace, Delia felt she had never seen Bay Borough in such detail -- every plastic cup lid wheeling along the sidewalk, every sparrow pecking tinfoil in the gutter." This detail was perfect for me, because I notice litter &amp; such one of the first times I walk through a new place. And so that's one way Delia and I differ - she's more focused on what's in front, what's significant, and I (as Tyler has made apparent) need to spend less time looking down and focusing on the negativity.<br /><br />I love that Delia, at age 40, discovered the library, and started borrowing books, instead of buying trashy romances. After a bit, well before she started reading classics, she isn't satisfied by the books she used to read. And when she is caught away and needs to buy a book, (because she finds TV exhausting, as do I) she buys "something serious and believable, about poor people in Maine." (Probably <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/263862.The_Beans_of_Egypt__Maine" title="The Beans of Egypt, Maine by Carolyn Chute" rel="nofollow noopener">The Beans of Egypt, Maine</a>**)<br /><br />Btw, I'll save you some research (if you want, but I'll hide it in spoilers if you don't. Very early on we learn that Delia's name is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Cordelia, and when a character asks if she's "her father's Cordelia" he is referring to the youngest daughter of King Lear.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> And the song Delia's father sang to her as a lullaby is <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[something I'd consider entirely inappropriate, by Johnny Cash: <br />Delia's Gone<br />Delia, oh, Delia Delia all my life<br />If I hadn't have shot poor<br />Delia I'd have had her for my wife<br />Delia's gone, one more round Delia's gone<br />I went up to Memphis<br />And I met Delia there Found her in her parlor<br />And I tied to her chair<br />Delia's gone, one more round Delia's gone<br />She was low down and trifling<br />And she was cold and mean<br />Kind of evil make me want to Grab my sub machine<br />Delia's gone, one more round Delia's gone<br />First time I shot her I shot her in the side<br />Hard to watch her suffer<br />But with the second shot she died<br />Delia's gone, one more round Delia's gone<br />But jailer, oh, jailer Jailer,<br />I can't sleep 'Cause all around my bedside<br />I hear the patter of Delia's feet<br />Delia's gone, one more round Delia's gone<br />So if you woman's devilish<br />You can let her run<br />Or you… Full lyrics on Google Play <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />And probably one of my favorite passages (even though, if over-analyzed, it can certainly be rendered meaningless):<br />"Oh, the <i>otherness</i> of Delia's children never failed to entrance her! She considered it a sort of bonus gift -- a means of experiencing, up close, an entirely opposite way of being."<br /><br />*Some readers' reviews question the ending. Do *not* read the spoiler if you have *any* intention of reading this book. Even after you've read it, think about the ending, come to your own conclusion, before reading what I figured out: <br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[The idea is that she owes her first allegiance to her own family - and that she's come to realize they do need, and deserve, her. And that she does love them. Noah and Joel will be ok. Maybe even Ellie will come back - she was advised to by Delia, remember, when she confessed to D. that she wonders if she'd made a mistake, and that she missed them.<br />I imagine, based on clues in the text, that she'll visit Bay B. sometimes. And folks back there may visit her... after all, Nat did in his hour of need. She'll not just run away like she did the year before. <br />I think I was able to read carefully because I empathized. I am actually, embarrassingly, on my third marriage. I'm a slow learner - so I wanted to pay attention to this story and learn how Delia made her choice. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />** Well, researching that cleared up a confusion that's been lurking in the back of my mind. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/263862.The_Beans_of_Egypt__Maine" title="The Beans of Egypt, Maine by Carolyn Chute" rel="nofollow noopener">The Beans of Egypt, Maine</a> is *not* <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30868.The_Bean_Trees__Greer_Family___1_" title="The Bean Trees (Greer Family, #1) by Barbara Kingsolver" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bean Trees</a>, though they do both have something to do with rural poverty. Yay for me figuring that out."</span>
  <a data-text-id="5414729161217047472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Tundra" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43990165-tundra"><img alt="Tundra" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593320700p2/43990165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3137457428?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tundra" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tundra" href="/user/show/43990165-tundra">Tundra</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780143012412" href="/book/show/1083361-ladder-of-years">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3137457428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16323888684893481045">An insightful examination of the ways in which personal identity and worth can be lost and regained through the choices that women make entering and leaving relationships. As always Anne Tyler makes the ordinary small moments of life significant and carefully shines a beam on what makes us human.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2512141724" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2512141724" />
    <a title="Lydia Bailey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/45167722-lydia-bailey"><img alt="Lydia Bailey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541061199p2/45167722.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2512141724?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lydia Bailey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lydia Bailey" href="/user/show/45167722-lydia-bailey">Lydia Bailey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2512141724" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8843219849140971608">Anne Tyler books are a bit like life itself; nothing much seems to happen day to day/ page to page but when you look back, a whole lot has changed. It took me an age to read this (just due to life interruptions) and it is slow paced. But this is usual for AT and it takes an adjustment to get back to reading that way. It’s not my favourite plot of hers but I love her writing, her way of depicting the realities of being human in general & being female in particular.<br/><br/> I particularly loved her observ</span>
  <span id="freeText8843219849140971608" style="display:none">Anne Tyler books are a bit like life itself; nothing much seems to happen day to day/ page to page but when you look back, a whole lot has changed. It took me an age to read this (just due to life interruptions) and it is slow paced. But this is usual for AT and it takes an adjustment to get back to reading that way. It’s not my favourite plot of hers but I love her writing, her way of depicting the realities of being human in general &amp; being female in particular.<br /><br /> I particularly loved her observations of parenting children who are now young adults &amp; that at the same time you’re often dealing with ageing parents, “ didn’t it often happen, she thought, that aged parents die exactly at the moment when other people (your husband, your adolescent children) have stopped being thrilled to see you? But a parent is always thrilled, always dwells so lovingly on your face as you are speaking. One of life’s little ironies.” <br /><br />Definitely one which will stay with me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8843219849140971608" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IrmnpbOCCB/tSBlo02wXN96WLyZN3+TJ6S2KjH+fkWTT+mpsSZM6L+6QJyx02qZaZAfV7y5dsNhSMQilUyiMQA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('TDoACnYDW9K686PAF/X6UnhthbMmODFnGHNwFKvCoKW9ec3DjBJp4rkrnYSwQ0s/wvx/ekW6ZXajb/I9h3W9gQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1933663428233675790">Anne Tyler was born in Minneapolis, Minnesota, in 1941 and grew up in Raleigh, North Carolina. She graduated at nineteen from Duke University and went on to do graduate work in Russian studies at Columbia University. She has published 20 novels, her debut novel being <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112321.If_Morning_Ever_Comes' title='If Morning Ever Comes' rel='nofollow noopener'>If Morning Ever Comes</a>
</i> in (1964). Her eleventh novel, <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31181.Breathing_Lessons' title='Breathing Lessons' rel='nofollow noopener'>Breathing Lessons</a>
</i>, was awarded the Pulitzer Prize in 1988. She is a mem</span>
  <span id="freeText1933663428233675790" style="display:none">Anne Tyler was born in Minneapolis, Minnesota, in 1941 and grew up in Raleigh, North Carolina. She graduated at nineteen from Duke University and went on to do graduate work in Russian studies at Columbia University. She has published 20 novels, her debut novel being <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/112321.If_Morning_Ever_Comes" title="If Morning Ever Comes" rel="nofollow noopener">If Morning Ever Comes</a>
</i> in (1964). Her eleventh novel, <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/31181.Breathing_Lessons" title="Breathing Lessons" rel="nofollow noopener">Breathing Lessons</a>
</i>, was awarded the Pulitzer Prize in 1988. She is a member of the American Academy of Arts and Letters.</span>
